Objection: Why Only Perception?
Answer to the objection about limiting to perception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the definition of life mentions only perception, even though life is also a condition for other attributes like power and will, through the principle of entailment and the 'condition of a condition'.

Core Idea
Life is the condition for all attributes because it is the condition for perception, which itself is a condition for others.

An attentive student might ask: since life is also a condition for attributes like power and will, why does the definition restrict itself to perception? The author provides a sophisticated answer based on the logical relationship between these attributes. This lesson explains that answer.

Guided Path
1
Raise the objection
The objection states that life is a condition for other attributes like power, will, and speech, not just perception. So why limit the definition to perception alone?
Read the objection carefully in the Arabic text.
2
Understand the answer via entailment (luzum)
The author answers that attributes like power and will actually entail perception. Since life is a condition for perception, it becomes a condition for whatever entails perception (the entailing thing). This is a logical principle: the condition of the entailed is a condition for the entailing thing.
Power, will, and speech are 'malzum' (entailing) and perception is 'lazim' (entailed).
3
Understand the alternative: condition of a condition
Another way: power and will require knowledge, and knowledge is a type of perception. Since life is a condition for knowledge (perception), it becomes a condition for power and will because the condition of a condition is a condition.
This is summarized as 'شرط الشرط شرط'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم الإلهيات: صفة تصحح لمن قامت به أن يتصف بصفات الإدراك. وجودها وجود الإدراك ولا عدمه، والمراد من تجويزها ذلك عدم الاستحالة، والمعنى على هذا: أنَّ عند وجود الحياة لا يستحيل الاتصاف بصفات الإدراك، والاتصاف بصفات الإدراك عند وجود الحياة ممكن بالإمكان العام الذي يشمل الواجب والمُستوي الطرفين، وحينئذ يجعل الاتصاف بالإدراك عند وجود الحياة بالنسبة إلى الحوادث مستوي الطرفين، وبالنسبة إلى القديم سبحانه واجبا، والحاصل: أنَّ كلمة «تصحح» الواقعة في هذا التعريف معناها بالنظر إلى القديم توجب له سبحانه أن يتصف بالإدراك أزلاً وأبدا؛ لأن كل ما صح في حقه تعالى فهو واجب، ومعناها بالنظر إلى الحوادث: تُجوِّز أن يتصف بالإدراك، ألا ترى حالة أنا قد نكون في نوم أو غفلة؟ فيكون الإدراك غير موجود وإن كانت الحياة موجودة. وإِنَّما قال: «تصحح لمن قامت به أن يتصف بصفات الإدراك» دون أن يقول: «تصحح لمن قامت به أن يدرك»؛ لأنَّ الذي من لوازم الحياة صحة الإدراك لا الإدراك نفسه، والإدراك ههنا يشمل: العلم، والسمع، والبصر، وغيرها. فإن قلت: فالحياة شرط للاتصاف بغير الإدراك من الصفات، كالقدرة، والإرادة، والكلام، فإنَّ كلَّ واحدة من هذه الصفات يستحيل وجودها بغير الحياة، فلماذا اقتصر على ذكر الإدراك؟ قلت: إِنَّ كون الحياة شرطًا للاتصاف بغير الإدراك من الصفات يُفهم بطريق اللزوم، وذلكَ لأنَّ القُدرة والإرادة والكلام وهذه صفات ملزومة للإدراك، وكل ما كان شرطًا في حصول اللازم فهو البَتَّةَ شرط في حصول الملزوم، فاقتصاره على ذكر الإدراك؛ لكونه يَستَتبع ما ذكرتَ مِن الصِّفات، وبعبارة أخرى: إنَّ القدرة والإرادة وغيرهما من الصفات لا تتحقق إلَّا بالعلم، فالعلم شرطٌ فيها، وجعل الحياة شرطًا في الاتصاف بالعلم، يستدعي كونها شرطًا في الاتصاف بالصِّفاتِ الأخرى، لأنَّ شرط الشرط شرط. ومن العلماء من عرَّف الحياة القديمة التي هي صفة الله تعالى بتعريف، وعرّف الحياة الحادثة صفة للحوادث بتعريف آخر، فعرّف الحياة القديمة بأنها: «صفةٌ أزليَّة تقتضي العلم»، أي: تقتضي صحة الاتّصاف بالعلم، وكما تقتضي صحة الاتصاف بالعلم تقتضي صحة الاتصاف بغيره من الصفات الواجبة له تعالى، وقد عرفت وجه ذلك كله فيما تقدَّم، وعرف الحياة الحادثة بأنها: «كيفيَّةٌ يَلزَمُها قَبُولُ الحِس والحركة الإرادية»، وقد سلك الشارح صحة هذا المسلك.
The Section on Divine Matters: An attribute that makes correct for the one in whom it subsists to be described with attributes of perception. Its existence is the existence of perception and not its non-existence, and the intended meaning of its making permissible is the absence of impossibility. The meaning based on this is that when life exists, being described with attributes of perception is not impossible, and being described with attributes of perception when life exists is possible with the general possibility that includes the obligatory and the two-sided equal. At that point, being described with perception when life exists is made two-sided equal with respect to originated things, and with respect to the Eternal, Exalted is He, obligatory. The conclusion is that the word 'makes correct' occurring in this definition, its meaning with respect to the Eternal necessitates for Him, Exalted is He, to be described with perception eternally and forever, because everything that is correct in His right, Exalted is He, is obligatory. Its meaning with respect to originated things is that it makes permissible that they be described with perception. Do you not see the case where we may be in sleep or heedlessness? Perception is non-existent even though life exists. He only said: 'makes correct for the one in whom it subsists to be described with attributes of perception' and did not say 'makes correct for the one in whom it subsists to perceive', because that which is entailed by life is the correctness of perception, not perception itself. Perception here includes: knowledge, hearing, sight, and others. If you say: Life is a condition for being described with other than perception from the attributes, such as power, will, and speech, for each of these attributes is impossible in existence without life, so why did he limit to mentioning perception? I answer: Indeed, life being a condition for being described with other than perception from the attributes is understood by way of entailment, because power, will, and speech are attributes that entail perception, and whatever is a condition for obtaining the entailed thing is absolutely a condition for obtaining the entailing thing. So his restriction to mentioning perception is because it entails those attributes you mentioned. In other words, power, will, and others are not realized except through knowledge, so knowledge is a condition for them. And making life a condition for being described with knowledge necessitates it being a condition for being described with the other attributes, because the condition of a condition is a condition. Some scholars defined the eternal life which is the attribute of Allah Most High with one definition, and defined the temporal life as an attribute of originated things with another definition. They defined eternal life as: 'An eternal attribute that necessitates knowledge,' i.e., it necessitates the correctness of being described with knowledge, and just as it necessitates the correctness of being described with knowledge, it necessitates the correctness of being described with other than it of the attributes obligatory for Him Most High. You have known the face of all that in what preceded. And they defined temporal life as: 'A quality which necessitates the reception of sense and voluntary motion.' And the commentator has followed this path.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage defines the divine attribute of life and explains its meaning. It begins with the definition: life is an attribute that makes correct for the one in whom it subsists to be described with attributes of perception. The author then unpacks the word 'tusahhih' (makes correct): for God, whatever is correct is necessary, so life entails actual perception eternally; for creatures, it merely permits perception, as seen in sleep where life exists but perception does not. The definition says 'attributes of perception' rather than 'perception' because life entails the correctness (sihha) of perception, not perception itself. Perception includes knowledge, hearing, sight, etc. An objection is raised: why mention only perception when life is also a condition for attributes like power, will, and speech? The answer is that these attributes actually entail perception, so life being a condition for perception makes it a condition for them by entailment (luzum). Alternatively, power and will require knowledge, and knowledge is a type of perception; thus condition of condition applies. Finally, the passage presents alternative definitions distinguishing eternal life (an eternal attribute necessitating knowledge) and temporal life (a quality necessitating sense reception and voluntary motion), noting that the commentator followed this path.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the definition is incomplete or arbitrary because it only mentions perception.
Correction: The definition implicitly covers all attributes that depend on perception through logical entailment and the condition-of-condition principle.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does life being a condition for knowledge make it a condition for power and will?

B) Because knowledge is a condition for power and will, and the condition of a condition is a condition
C) Because life and power are the same
D) Because the author made a mistake

Key Takeaway

?

Alternative Definitions: Eternal and Temporal Life
Alternative definitions of eternal and temporal life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two distinct definitions some scholars give for eternal life (attribute of Allah) and temporal life (attribute of creatures).

Core Idea
Eternal life necessitates knowledge; temporal life necessitates sense and motion.

Some scholars prefer to define life differently for the Creator and for creatures. For Allah, life is an eternal attribute that necessitates the correctness of knowledge. For creatures, life is a quality that necessitates sense reception and voluntary motion. This lesson presents these alternative definitions and notes the commentator's preference.

Guided Path
1
Read the two definitions
Read the Arabic definitions for eternal life and temporal life. Note their distinct phrasing: eternal life is 'an eternal attribute that necessitates knowledge', temporal life is 'a quality which necessitates the reception of sense and voluntary motion'.
Eternal life is specific to Allah; temporal life is for created beings.
2
Understand why eternal life necessitates knowledge
The commentator clarifies that 'necessitates knowledge' means it necessitates the correctness of being described with knowledge, and by extension, other obligatory attributes. This aligns with the earlier discussion about life entailing correctness of perception.
The earlier definition used 'makes correct'; this one uses 'necessitates'.
3
Understand the definition of temporal life
Temporal life is defined as a quality that necessitates the ability to receive sense impressions and perform voluntary motion. This is a common definition in kalam for the life of animals and humans.
This definition focuses on observable effects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Life's Unique Relation: The Ash'ari Position on Divine Attributes
Debate on whether life is related to something and the nature of its relation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'ari school holds that the attribute of life has no relation to anything external, unlike other attributes of meanings.

Core Idea
Life's attribute has no external relation; it only subsists in the essence.

This passage delves into a critical distinction among God's attributes of meanings (sifat al-ma'ani). While most attributes like power, will, and knowledge require an object (e.g., known, willed), life is unique in that it does not entail anything beyond the essence. The discussion explores the nature of this 'relation' (ta'luq) and whether it is essential or merely conceptual.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim about life
Read the opening lines: 'Life is not related to anything because it does not entail an additional matter beyond subsistence in its locus.' This is the central thesis.
Notice how the author contrasts life with power, will, etc.
2
Understand the distinction between attributes with and without relation
The passage explains that attributes that have a relation (like power and knowledge) require an extra object beyond their subsistence. Life lacks this, making it a unique attribute.
3
Examine the multiple opinions on the nature of the relation
The passage lists views: (1) al-Ash'ari says it's essential (nafsi), (2) some say it's a relative matter (i'tibari), (3) others that only God knows it, and (4) that relation is an existential attribute (refuted).
Focus on why the fourth view is refuted.
4
Distinguish eternal relation from temporal relation
The author distinguishes the eternal essential relation (which includes executionary and conditional) from temporal relation, emphasizing that the essential relation is eternal and unchanging.

وأما أن هذه الصفة تتعلق بشيء أو لا تتعلق ؟ فنقول: إن صفة الحياة لا تتعلق بشيء، وذلك لأنها لا تستلزم أمراً زائداً على القيام بمحلها ، والصِّفةُ التي تتعلق بشيءٍ هي التي تستلزم أمرًا بعد قيامه بمحله ـ يطلب أمرًا يُعلَم به ؟ وكذا الاقتصاد زائداً على القيام بمحلها ، ألا ترى أنَّ القدرة والإرادة ونحوهما. العلم - ومن الذي قدمناه في ذكر ما تتعلق به الصفاتُ تَعلَم أَنَّ جميعَ صِفات المعاني متعلّقة، أي: طالبةٌ لزائد على القيام بمحالها ، إلَّا الحياة ؛ فإنها لا تتعلق بشيء، ونظيرُ الحياة القدم والبقاء عند من يجعلهما من صفات المعاني، وهذا التعلق نفسي لتلك الصفات، فلا توجد في صفة منها بدون تعلّقها، فتعلّقُ كلَّ صفةٍ بما تتعلّق به أزلي ، وكذلك قيام كل صفة دو الخارج منها بالذات نفسي، فلا توجد صفةٌ منها في الخارج قائمة بنفسها، بل توجد قائمة بالذَّاتِ، وما ذكرناه مِن أنَّ التَّعلَّقَ نفسي هو قول الأشعري ، وقيل : إنَّ كلا من تعلق الصفة وقيامها بالذات أمر اعتباري ، وإنه من قبيل النّسب والإضافات ، وقيل : إنه من مواقف العقول، أي: لا يعلمه إلا الله ، وقيل : إن تعلّق الصفة صفةٌ وجوديَّةٌ لها ، ورُدَّ هذا بأنَّه يستلزم قيامَ المعنَى بالمعنَى . واعلم أنَّ التَّعلَّق الموصوفَ بكونه نفسيَّا هو التَّعلَّق القديم، لا الحادث، لتحقق الصفة أزلا وأبدا بدون التعلق الحادث، والتّعلُّق القديم يشمل التَنْجِيزي القديم بالنسبة للعلم والإرادة والكلام، ويشمل الصلوحي القديم بالنسبة للقدرة والإرادة ، وليس خاصا بالصلوحي خلافا لبعضهم . محي .
As for whether this attribute is related to something or not, we say: The attribute of life is not related to anything, because it does not entail an additional matter beyond subsisting in its locus. The attribute that is related to something is the one that entails an additional matter after its subsistence in its locus — it seeks a matter by which it is known? And likewise power? additional to subsistence in its locus. Do you not see that power, will, and similar [attributes] — knowledge — and from what we have presented in what the attributes are related to, you know that all attributes of meanings are related, i.e., seek an additional matter beyond subsisting in their loci, except life; for it is not related to anything. The analogue of life is pre-eternity and everlastingness for those who consider them attributes of meanings. This relation is essential for those attributes, so not one of them exists without its relation. Thus the relation of each attribute to that to which it is related is eternal, and likewise the subsistence of each attribute in the essence is essential, so no attribute among them exists in the external subsisting by itself, rather it exists subsisting in the essence. What we have mentioned that relation is essential is the saying of al-Ash'ari. It is said that both the relation of the attribute and its subsistence in the essence are matters of consideration, and they are of the category of relations and additions. It is said that it is from the stop-points of intellects, i.e., no one knows it but Allah. It is said that the relation of the attribute is an existential attribute for it, and this is refuted because it entails the subsistence of a meaning in a meaning. Know that the relation described as essential is the eternal relation, not the temporal, because the attribute is realized eternally and forever without the temporal relation. The eternal relation includes the eternal executionary relation with respect to knowledge, will, and speech, and includes the eternal conditional relation with respect to power and will, and it is not specific to the conditional contrary to some. Muhi.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage discusses a key distinction among divine attributes: whether they have a relation (ta'luq) to something beyond the essence. The author states that life is unique in having no relation, because it does not entail anything beyond subsisting in its locus. In contrast, all other attributes of meanings (sifat al-ma'ani) such as power, will, and knowledge are related; they seek an additional object. The author then explains that this relation is essential (nafsi) for those attributes, meaning it is inherent and eternal, not accidental. He attributes this view to al-Ash'ari. Several other opinions are presented: (1) the relation is merely a relative matter (amr i'tibari) like relations and additions; (2) it is among the stop-points of intellects, known only to Allah; (3) the relation is an existential attribute itself, but this is refuted because it would lead to a meaning subsisting in a meaning. Finally, the author distinguishes eternal relation (which includes both tanjizi — executionary, and suluhi — conditional) from temporal relation, emphasizing that the essential relation is eternal and unchanging.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That life relates to objects like other attributes, implying life gives life to something external.
Correction: Life in God does not entail any external object; it is purely a perfection of the essence without requiring a recipient.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari view presented, what is the relation (ta'luq) of the attribute of life?
A) It is related to objects of knowledge
B) It is related to power and will
C) It is not related to anything
D) It is an existential attribute

Key Takeaway
Life's attribute does not relate to anything external; its only relation is essential subsistence in the divine essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, you attribute 'life' to yourself and to others—a life that constantly interacts with objects and circumstances. How does knowing that Allah's life has no relation to anything challenge the way you imagine His existence? Will you pause today to remind yourself that He is utterly self-sufficient, needing no object to be alive?
?
The passage insists that life's uniqueness among attributes means it does not 'seek' anything beyond itself. When you ask Allah for something, do you sometimes feel He needs your request to complete His will? How does the fact that His life is relation-less free you from thinking He lacks anything? Commit to thanking Him today for being absolutely independent of your actions.
?
The refuted opinion claimed that the relation of an attribute is itself an existential attribute. Have you ever treated God's attributes as if they were multiple distinct entities added to His essence? How does the Ash'ari insistence on essential, intrinsic relations—except for life—push you to a simpler, more unified understanding of His nature? What will you change in how you speak about His attributes starting now?
